<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_465010482">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/465010482" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3170403-alice" class="left imgcol" title="Alice"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1264378680p2/3170403.jpg" alt="Alice" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/465010482?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 27, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3170403-alice" class="user" title="Alice">Alice</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6878517-os-c-es-de-babel" title="Paperback 9789722342155" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3170403-alice?shelf=ed-presen%C3%A7a" class="actionLinkLite">ed-presença</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3170403-alice?shelf=2009" class="actionLinkLite">2009</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3170403-alice?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer465010482">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4164020121641633443">Está a partir de hoje disponível o romance que se tornou Bestseller mundial e que marca a estreia da autora Carolyn Parkhurst. Cães de Babel, é um comovente e marcante relato na primeira pessoa da dor indescritível que é perder alguém que amamos, dor essa que se torna insuportável quando temos a certeza de que há algo por explicar, algo que está tão mal como uma peça que não encaixa num puzzle que parecia perfeito.<br /><br />Tudo começa com a morte de Lexy que para a polícia não passa de um terrível aciden</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4164020121641633443">Está a partir de hoje disponível o romance que se tornou Bestseller mundial e que marca a estreia da autora Carolyn Parkhurst. Cães de Babel, é um comovente e marcante relato na primeira pessoa da dor indescritível que é perder alguém que amamos, dor essa que se torna insuportável quando temos a certeza de que há algo por explicar, algo que está tão mal como uma peça que não encaixa num puzzle que parecia perfeito.<br /><br />Tudo começa com a morte de Lexy que para a polícia não passa de um terrível acidente embora o seu marido Paul não pense da mesma forma. Seguindo pequenas "pistas" aparentemente deixadas pela própria Lexy, Paul inicia uma investigação que o levará a uma apaixonante viagem pelos recônditos caminhos da memória dando-nos a conhecer a sua vida e o seu casamento mas sobretudo a artista imprevisível com quem era casado. É esta viagem ao seu interior que nos revela as confusões de um coração toldado pela dor e a dura realidade presente em cada um de nós - todo o ser humano têm inúmeras facetas guardadas no seu interior, segredos, pequenos pensamentos e sentimentos que guarda para si e apenas para si; na verdade não conhecemos tão bem e tão profundamente quanto pensamos aqueles que amamos.<br /><br />A escrita é profunda e tocante mas ao mesmo tempo carinhosa e simples, repleta de humor e sobretudo de amor, levando o leitor a tentar compreender as incertezas e a dor causadas pela morte de alguém que nos é querido e o penoso caminho que tem que ser trilhado para alcançar a aceitação do sucedido e, no caso de Paul, o perdão que trarão alguma paz de espírito.<br />Não me espantaria ver esta obra adaptada ao grande ecrã num filme bem ao jeito de As palavras que nunca te direi. Recomendo.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4164020121641633443">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer323153628">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17813060610271324955">This book wasn't what I was expecting at all. I guess I was expecting something more along the lines of The Art of Racing In The Rain where the dog, Lorelei, had a more prominent and endearing role. I wasn't expecting what did happen in the book and how Paul tried to get her to talk. I couldn't connect with any character in the book. I did understand Paul's grief and why he needed to know if his wife Lexy's death was an accident or not but the author just took everything too far. By the end I wa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17813060610271324955">This book wasn't what I was expecting at all. I guess I was expecting something more along the lines of The Art of Racing In The Rain where the dog, Lorelei, had a more prominent and endearing role. I wasn't expecting what did happen in the book and how Paul tried to get her to talk. I couldn't connect with any character in the book. I did understand Paul's grief and why he needed to know if his wife Lexy's death was an accident or not but the author just took everything too far. By the end I was just skimming to see what happened. I wouldn't recommend this to anyone. There are just too many other better books out there and after looking at the reviews and descriptions of Parkhurst's other novels I don't think I will be giving her another try. This just wasn't very good. I'm glad I got this book basically for free on PaperBackSwap.com because it definitely isn't worth wasting even a penny on. Sorry for such a bad review but this was a bad book...at least for me. 1 star. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16595915167712756189">I couldn't decide between 4 stars or 5, so I decided to be generous and go with 5.<br /><br />Ultimately this is a stunningly beautiful love story, but it remains rooted in reality.<br /><br />Paul learns that his wife has died falling out of an apple tree.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText16595915167712756189">I couldn't decide between 4 stars or 5, so I decided to be generous and go with 5.<br /><br />Ultimately this is a stunningly beautiful love story, but it remains rooted in reality.<br /><br />Paul learns that his wife has died falling out of an apple tree. The death is discovered because Lorelei (their dog) is making horrible noises in the back yard. The Police tell him it looks like an accident, but they have to rule out suicide. After a brief discussion with Paul, and with the position of the body, it is determined that her death is an accident. Later, Paul discovers incongruities. He sees she cooked a steak, but did not use any dishes for it, and there is evidence of the steak being on the floor. Paul realizes that the only witness to the death is Lorelei, and decides he needs to find a way to help Lorelei communicate with him.<br /><br />This is a novel about grief, loss, love and beauty.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38960224">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5769065589714013131">Why do we give one book 5 stars and another 4? I would have to say this one intrigued me from the moment I found it at the library in the used book sale. No one had read it, the pages hadn't even been flipped through, but the small bit I read made it impossible for me to put it down. I found it heart breakingly sad and beautiful at once. I give it 5 stars over 4 because it was written in a way that felt like waves on the shore. It rushes forward with the current story, it pulls back with the fla</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5769065589714013131">Why do we give one book 5 stars and another 4? I would have to say this one intrigued me from the moment I found it at the library in the used book sale. No one had read it, the pages hadn't even been flipped through, but the small bit I read made it impossible for me to put it down. I found it heart breakingly sad and beautiful at once. I give it 5 stars over 4 because it was written in a way that felt like waves on the shore. It rushes forward with the current story, it pulls back with the flashbacks. Each rush forward takes you closer to the end of the book, yet each flashback became more and more engaging. I was never bored, never irritated and although the beginning premise was farfetched, it was written so well that you can't say, "Oh, give me a break!". Well, maybe you could, but I never did. A truly beautiful read for me.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/1161614-veronica" class="user" title="Veronica">Veronica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Veronica by: </span>
      Abby Carr
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1161614-veronica?shelf=2009" class="actionLinkLite">2009</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1161614-veronica?shelf=adult-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">adult-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer56660232">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6620078719880755594">This was a book I could not put down. In <em>The Dogs of Babel</em>, a linguist by the name of Paul Iverson becomes obsessed with the seemingly accidental death of his wife. Alone at home, she fell from a tree with their Rhodesian Ridgeback as the only witness to the horrific scene, leaving Paul with nothing but unanswered questions and unverified suspicions. Spurred by his grief and a few "incongruities" that he believes may hold the key to the uncovering his wife's motives on that final day, he begins</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6620078719880755594">This was a book I could not put down. In <em>The Dogs of Babel</em>, a linguist by the name of Paul Iverson becomes obsessed with the seemingly accidental death of his wife. Alone at home, she fell from a tree with their Rhodesian Ridgeback as the only witness to the horrific scene, leaving Paul with nothing but unanswered questions and unverified suspicions. Spurred by his grief and a few "incongruities" that he believes may hold the key to the uncovering his wife's motives on that final day, he begins his quest to teach Lorelei (the dog) to speak. The emotions in this novel are so painfully human, so poignant and meaningful to the narrator that the reader cannot help but fall into the story. Five stars, only because I can't give it more... I <u>really</u> enjoyed this book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6620078719880755594">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_257392103">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257392103" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4776372-jennifer" class="left imgcol" title="Jennifer"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1389703103p2/4776372.jpg" alt="Jennifer" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/257392103?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 04, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4776372-jennifer" class="user" title="Jennifer">Jennifer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4776372-jennifer?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer257392103">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15523976609264158125">I wish I could give this book higher than a five. Or I wish I could go back to all the other books I've ever rated and knock them down a notch. Nothing I've read before quite matches up to this book. <br /><br />I browsed through some other ratings online, before I started reading the book, and was surprised at the amount of people who rolled their eyes at the topic. I immediately knew it was a good topic for me. So many times I've wanted to know what my own dogs were thinking, and I think it was a nice, fr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15523976609264158125">I wish I could give this book higher than a five. Or I wish I could go back to all the other books I've ever rated and knock them down a notch. Nothing I've read before quite matches up to this book. <br /><br />I browsed through some other ratings online, before I started reading the book, and was surprised at the amount of people who rolled their eyes at the topic. I immediately knew it was a good topic for me. So many times I've wanted to know what my own dogs were thinking, and I think it was a nice, fresh subject that hasn't been covered in every other book before. I think I was hooked before I even opened the book. Many people balked at the fact that Paul would try to teach his dog to talk, or that he would call a psychic. I immediately thought that he should call a pyschic, so none of this was shocking to me. <br /><br />I think the story was beautifully written. The only part I could have done without is the story about (and friends of) Hollis Wendel, but not because I don't think they add something to the book, but because I personally cannot handle any type of animal abuse. <br /><br />I loved the flashbacks into how Lexy and Paul met and how they became married, and all the flashbacks into their marriage. I think it really leant something special to the book, though I will admit that sometimes I just wanted to get back to the story at hand just beause it was so good or it was at that special point where you just have to know what happens next. But take that with a grain of salt, it's not that the flashbacks weren't good and weren't worth reading, just that I was so drawn in by the story, that I would think, "Can't we put off this flahsback for a chapter or two until I find out what happens to...?" <br /><br />The cover of the book says it rises to a point of stirring, peaceful grace, and I hoped I would know when that point was, and of course I did. I wish I could say it was as peaceful for me though. It wasn't. I haven't cried over a book in years and didn't expect to anytime soon. I think I've never gotten to "know" the characters as deeply as felt I knew Paul, Lexy, and Lorelei. I started crying when Paul found out what Lorelei was trying to say all along. I started crying again when he finally found out what the books meant. I started crying again when I found out the importance of the steak. My heart broke more than once for Lorelei, not only when you find out what she did for Lexy (when Paul decided to see what the view was like), but also, for how she must have felt when she got out of that doggy door. She must have been confused and scared, and I just wanted to be there to console her. I know how odd this all sounds. Again, I can only stress just how entrancced I was by this story. I will also confess that a lot of my tears stemmed from my own fears and wondering how I could continue to go on if I were to lose my husband. It seems unfathonable, and in that way, my heart also broke for Paul, for Lexy, who got to "that" point, and for the love that they shared and was lost. <br /><br />At the end of the book, after deciding not to open the front cover and start reading it all over again, I thought about starting a different book, even though I'd already been reading for four hours and it was almost midnight, and way too late for me, but I just couldn't do it. I felt it would be "disrespectful" to how amazing this book was, and I know that may seem odd, but all I can say is that I got to the point where I thought Paul and Lexy and Lorelei were real people out there somewhere and my heart broke for their story. I've never been touched by a book like this before. I had to keep reminding myself after I'd finished reading it, that this was a book of fiction, and there was no reason for me to be so upset. <br /><br />In the end, I didn't go back to the first page and start again, and I do plan on picking up another book today, but none of them quite seem worth reading anymore. It's that feeling when you finish such an amazing book, you just know no other will ever be able to top it, and so you're no longer as excited about reading them anymore. I am though, going to hold onto this book, as I think one day at some point I'm going to start from the beginning again.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15523976609264158125">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer36729239">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4427723109203271200">Paul Iverson returns home one day to find his wife, Lexy Ransome, dead from a fall from a tree in their back yard. Their dog, Lorelei, was the only witness. Bereft at the loss of his beloved, Paul tries to learn the story of her death from the only witness to the event, Lorelei. He takes a sabbatical from his teaching position, determined to teach Lorelei to communicate. His life becomes an obsession. Parkhurst reveals, in flashback, Paul and Lexy’s relationship, showing the signs of trouble as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4427723109203271200">Paul Iverson returns home one day to find his wife, Lexy Ransome, dead from a fall from a tree in their back yard. Their dog, Lorelei, was the only witness. Bereft at the loss of his beloved, Paul tries to learn the story of her death from the only witness to the event, Lorelei. He takes a sabbatical from his teaching position, determined to teach Lorelei to communicate. His life becomes an obsession. Parkhurst reveals, in flashback, Paul and Lexy’s relationship, showing the signs of trouble as well as the moments of splendor. Paul finds clues and tries to see what they tell him. Was her death an accident or not? He goes too far, beginning to fall apart, his home becoming a shocking hovel, his mind willing to speak with unspeakable people in his search for answers. We learn of Lorelei’s origins as well as Lexy’s end. <br /><br />There was a particularly moving passage that hit a strong note for me<br /><br />P 78<br />Suicide is just a moment…For just a moment it doesn’t matter that you’ve got people who love you and the sun is shining and there’s a movie coming out this weekend that you’ve been dying to see. It hits you all of a sudden that nothing is ever going to be okay, ever, and you kind of dare yourself: Is this it? You start thinking that you’ve known this was coming all along, but you don’t know if today’s going to be the day. And if you think about it too much, it’s probably not. But you dare yourself. You pick up a knife and press it gently to your skin, you look out a nineteenth story window and you think, I could just do it. And most of the time, you look at the height and you get scared, or you think about the poor people on the sidewalk below—what if there are kids coming home from school and they have to spend the rest of their lives trying to forget this terrible thing you’re going to make them see? And the moment over. You think about how sad it would have been if you never got to see that movie, and you look at your dog and wonder who would’ve taken care of her if you had gone. And you go back to normal. But you keep it there in your mind. Even if you never take yourself up on it, it gives you a kind of comfort to know that the day is yours to choose. You tuck it away in your brain like sour candy tucked into your cheek, and the puckering memory it leaves behind, the rough pleasure of running your tongue over its strange terrain, is exactly the same.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4427723109203271200">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer517293853">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10274092668980055636">This is the May-December romance between a cardboard cut-out of Eeyore, "the sad donkey," and the wife he obsesses over, the dream diary of a 14-year-old Manic Pixie Dream Girl. Follow these 2D characters as they ride what looks to be an interesting sheep from the book flap but is actually one ugly wolf of shallow melodrama.<br /><br />I rarely feel so insulted and disgusted by a book, but everything about Dogs of Babel feels like lies. We've all experienced grief and the feeling of isolation and perhaps ev</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10274092668980055636">This is the May-December romance between a cardboard cut-out of Eeyore, "the sad donkey," and the wife he obsesses over, the dream diary of a 14-year-old Manic Pixie Dream Girl. Follow these 2D characters as they ride what looks to be an interesting sheep from the book flap but is actually one ugly wolf of shallow melodrama.<br /><br />I rarely feel so insulted and disgusted by a book, but everything about Dogs of Babel feels like lies. We've all experienced grief and the feeling of isolation and perhaps even suicidal thoughts, darkness of which Parkhurst claims expose the very depths. But there's nothing there. A lazy mystery led by hollow shells of characters endlessly attempting even hollower jokes.<br /><br />If you enjoy being subjected to meandering, sketchy retellings of some ditz's dreams, complete with anomaly-hunting, this book is for you. At least while Parkhurst patiently follows her characters through a bookful of such irrational grasping at straws she doesn't succumb, but that doesn't make the journey worthwhile.</span>

In doing so, Jo must leave behind her home and her best friend Jack, and risk losing him forever.In Florence, Jo’s intense artistic visions begin to find fruition, but her odyssey is complicated when she meets Chad and Walter, two extraordinary young men.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/34061.Carolyn_Parkhurst">About Carolyn Parkhurst</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/34061.Carolyn_Parkhurst"><img alt="34061" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1255518333p2/34061.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer3920473307581689160">Carolyn Parkhurst is an American author who has published two books. Her first, the 2003 best-seller The Dogs of Babel, was a New York Times Notable Book. She followed that effort with Lost and Found in June 2006.<br /><br />Parkhurst received her B.A. degree from Wesleyan University and an M.F.A. in Creative Writing from American University. <br /><br />She currently resides in Washington, D.C.<br /></span>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/trivia/work/1585061-the-dogs-of-babel">Trivia About The Dogs Of Babel</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
        <div class="mediumText">
          4 trivia questions 
          <br />
           
        </div>
        <a href="/trivia/work/1585061-the-dogs-of-babel" style="float: right;" class="actionLink">More quizzes &amp; trivia...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1585061-the-dogs-of-babel">Quotes from The Dogs of Babel</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Suicide is just a moment, Lexy told me. This is how she described it to me. For just a moment, it doesn't matter that you've got people who love you and the sun is shining and there's a movie coming out this weekend that you've been dying to see. It hits you all of a sudden that nothing is ever going to be okay, ever, and you kind of dare yourself. You pick up a knife and press it gently to your skin, you look out a nineteenth-story window and you think, I could just do it. I could just do it. And most of the time, you look at the height and you get scared, or you think about the poor people on the sidewalk below - what if there are kids coming home from school and they have to spend the rest of their lives trying to forget this terrible thing you're going to make them see? And the moment's over. You think about how sad it would've been if you never got to see that movie, and you look at your dog and wonder who would've taken care of her if you had gone. And you go back to normal. But you keep it there in your mind. Even if you never take yourself up on it, it gives you a kind of comfort to know that the day is yours to choose. You tuck it away in your brain like sour candy tucked in your cheek, and the puckering memory it leaves behind, the rough pleasure of running your tongue over its strange terrain, is exactly the same.... The day was hers to choose, and perhaps in that treetop moment when she looked down and saw the yard, the world, her life, spread out below her, perhaps she chose to plunge toward it headlong. Perhaps she saw before her a lifetime of walking on the ruined earth and chose instead a single moment in the air”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/62558-suicide-is-just-a-moment-lexy-told-me-this-is" class="actionLinkLite">175 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“The conclusion I have reached is that, above all, dogs are witnesses. They are allowed access to our most private moments. They are there when we think we are alone. Think of what they could tell us. They sit on the laps of presidents. They see acts of love and violence, quarrels and feuds, and the secret play of children. If they could tell us everything they have seen, all of the gaps of our lives would stitch themselves together.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/126925-the-conclusion-i-have-reached-is-that-above-all-dogs" class="actionLinkLite">79 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a href="/work/quotes/1585061-the-dogs-of-babel" style="float: right" class="actionLink">More quotes…</a>
